This creamery was pretty busy with an after lunch rush on Saturday, that being said after ordering my friends and I got our ice cream about half an hour later. We stopped in here yesterday and got a couple scoops in the afternoon. Our timing was right because demands was so high during the heat wave that they actually ran out! I chatted with the gentleman running the place after he closed the doors - they even ordered extra dairy this weekend in anticipation of the extra business, but still didn't have enough! I had the Nutella-flavored ice cream, and my +1 had a vanilla/cake mix called AB2. Both were fantastic. The lettuce is pretty reasonable for gourmet ice cream at Fashion Island. < Text>
Walked in 1st visit. Small frontage order area, register to the right small bit of counter seating to the left. Kind of like a Creamisry with fresher ingredients. The concept is to use top notch ingredients and create ice cream using the nitrogen process. It's an old chemistry class trick that when done right using their custom machines, makes very smooth ice cream. Ok, regarding the smoothness, straight up I'd be back in a heartbeat for the product. As for price the website looks like no update since March 2018 (?) We were able to order the Lil Bites (?) maybe used to be Lil Scientists. This is a limited menu of smaller sized, but less expensive choices @ 4.50$/ea. This choice was a value and as a dinner dessert plenty for portion size. A few downsides... We ordered thinking we were first to be served. With only two ice cream machines in use, there were actually two orders ahead of us. We didn't want to seem impatient, but our order was ready 20+ minutes after ring up. Be cautious if you are going to a movie, etc. There was what looked like three young staff and one Supervisor/Mgr on shift to make orders. With orders coming in I did not see the machine bowls filled, churning out ice cream. I have no clue what wait time is when they have a rush but I'm sure it's more than 20+ minutes. There was the usual pop music medium volume in the store. Hip n cool, yes, but bummer the staff was shouting over the combo of music and the air blasts the nitrogen made as it hit the mixing bowl. I didn't care to much for one employee discussing work hours and employee habits while making the ice cream. As first time customers, I thought the register/counter person could have been more helpful or friendly to us. The girl at the "finishing" station was moving a bit slow compared to back service restuarant people I've worked with. Again as commented only one machine of two was used on average, sometimes two. Magically, they did get orders out in a roughly smooth operation. There was a looseness to the group for example a woman came in and just waited at the register for service for quite some time before being noticed. The place was very clean as expected. A little bit of old ice cream and toppings floating in the dipper wells. I did notice an employee rinsing blades in the dipper wells instead of being sanitized in the sink. Overall an average experience with very good ice cream. I can see this is a good product by people with good intentions. FYI, I've managed and sold ice cream, not easy. My intent here is not to anonymously rip on a store. I hope they resolve the output issue to make more product faster but still keep quality. Also, I know it's a challenge to manage kids getting minimum wage, but they owe the company to represent the product and encourage people to come back. Leasing at Fashion Island is not cheap. Oh and its AUG 2018, keeping websites current is extra work on top of 14 hour days, I know I've worked them. But current info sells the awesome fresh ingredient model to a wider group of people for you... Thank you kindly for the great ice cream tonight.< /Text>

<Rating>3</Rating><user>112264597808775107784</user><text>Within my first  year of being a student at MSJC, I ran into several issues in regards to the professors. Some of our professors are too political, allowing one sided political discussion to take place within an academic platform. I prefer a college that restricts sexist and political comments, but mostly, I prefer to not be graded negatively for having to respond to these posts as a requirement for discussion boards and peer reviews. It's hard to stay neutral of all political issues when you are forced to respond/critique another student. I understand that this is a inevitable, thus me not basing this review solely off its political drama.
Another issue with MSJC is it's reliability for requirements to stay transparent within classes. Too often I have to navigate and surf through announcements to find an assignment that was not posted within the "Assignments" or "Grades" or even "Modules" tab. It's become a burden to not only have a higher work-load for a community college, but to have assignments due within 5 hours after seeing a late announcement... this leads to such interruption of family life that this school is simply not worth it.
If you are reading this comment and my complaints sound familiar to your experiences, just remember that the deans are very supportive to fixing your classes; It's just that no-one wants to place a complaint on their professor, especially since it's mostly an adjustment to a fully online  system.
Overall, this college has a strong VA support system, strong mathematics and science professors, and great administration in regards to deans. The main issue, as previously stated, is the reliability, the political tension, and the work-load for online-classes, where typically it's expected to be difficult to get a stronger education.

< review>
The newest super sport in the IE, not quite as elaborate as the north fontana facility but awesome none the less. The layout is nice, reminds me of a slightly larger scale version of the new la fitness facilities but with towel service. Dumbells up to 120lbs for all you buff guys and a trx machine which seems to be standard at the new supersports. Most of the pieces of cardio equipment have individual tvs on them and they even have some light kettle bells. The filtered water bottle refill stations are a cool new addition to the new supersports as well.</review>

< review>
Great place for great prices. Remember everybody, this is a discount store so the service is not the top. The service is actually very good for the price they charge. If you want great service than go to whole food and pay twice the price.

Lately, they have been carrying Asian produces and groceries. About 40% of the customers are Asian, its no longer a Hispanic market only.

The price for their meat is lower than even the Chinese market. They have the best prices for fruits and vegetables. Since there are so many shoppers they stuff are fresh.

The only criticism is that there is no Asian employee.  Since a big chunk of customers are Asian, they should seriously consider add some Chinese speaking employees.

Just be aware of Wednesday, it's the day of the sale in fruits and vegetables.  It could get very crowded.<//review>

< text>
Yes the prices are pretty good for fresh produce, and also in the meat department. But unless you're ready for a third world experience don't come here. People crowd the Isles leave their carts whereever ever they care to. Other items like soup and bread are very expensive here. So they lure you in with good prices on some items but price gouge you on other things.
The produce is third grade, meaning it's not perfect, has a few imperfections and such. There are multiple bins of grains and scoopable products, I don't recognize half of the items that I see. Come here for cheap produce and maybe some meat and call it a day. In general the clientele are oblivious to societal norms, expect to get jostled and bumped and scowled at when you come here.<//text>

<UserId.>108711041503232623591< /UserId.>< Name>
ella s.</Name>
<Time>1564803383133</Time><Rate>1< /Rate>< review>
This was originally posted on yelp but I am so incredibly angry with the experience I had today that I feel the need to repost here.

Zumiez does not even deserve one star. I just went into this store with my two friends but i'll never be coming back in here again.

We walked in only to be bombarded by at least 4 sales associates telling us about the deals, which we had to repeatedly hear about 4 separate times. It seems like they are really forcing help upon customers which makes me think they work on commission, but I'm not sure. We asked where the swimsuits were and the employee spent a few minutes asking other employees where they were before realizing they didn't sell any (weird). My friend picked up an air freshener that she planned on buying and went to the back of the store to look at the men's graphic tees to find something else to purchase with the air freshener.

At this point a fifth sales associate came and started complimenting my other friends chains, to a point of harassment.  He started to bring shirts for my friend to "compliment" his chains, and at this point we were so uncomfortable that my friend put down her air freshener on a pile of clothes and walked out, so she would not have to talk to other employees during the checkout process. It was annoying to say the least. I have never felt so pressured to buy clothes before.

We walked out of the store and this employee who was some sort of undercover loss protection (longish hair and in late 20s/early 30s, i hope she's reading this) comes running after us and holds her hand out and says "Air freshener?" as if assuming we stole the air freshener. At this point I realize the workers weren't even trying to be helpful, they were trying to make conversation to tell if we were trying to steal or not.  My friend said she "left it on a pile of clothes" because she DID. The worker said, in the most condescending tone may i add, "would you like to show me where you put it?" My friend showed her the table she left it on and the worker looked almost disappointed that she had been proven wrong. She proceeded to say, "next time hand the item to us or put it back where you got it from if you don't want it." When have you ever heard a retail employee say "put that back where you got it from"? The workers are getting paid to keep the store looking tidy, it's not the customer's job. And if it is the customer's job, Zumiez, maybe make sure your workers aren't so pushy they're repelling customers from the store. If Zumiez is trying to lose business they're doing a great job. There were also way too many workers standing around and trying to push deals, which just reminds me how much I hate coming to the mall.

If you didn't read the whole thing, here's the takeaways:
-way too many pushy employees.
-management is rude and condescending and obviously has nothing better to do than accuse teenagers of stealing.</review>

My garage has been damaged and unable to close or lock since March of this year (see attached picture), necessitating a replacement. Not only is this an eyesore for my neighbors and I, but there is also a real risk of theft of my belongings (including thousands of dollars’ worth of bicycles, camping equipment and cherished invaluable heirlooms). I am sure you are aware of the frequency of thefts occurring in the Woodbridge area, and it is obvious that my open garage is an easy target.

When I first became aware of the issue, I immediately notified my landlord. We had a garage repair company out to see what could be done, and we were told it would require replacement. My landlord promptly reported this to your board in mid-April. A contractor, Entry Systems, was sent out by the board to evaluate the garage, and also agreed that it required replacement. I am told by my landlord that in order to replace the door, approval must be obtained from your company.

My family and I have had nothing but problems and inconveniences while waiting for your approval to replace the door. One morning I left my house to go to work and I was unable to open my garage at all, which prevented me from getting my car out.  I am a registered nurse and, needless to say, during this pandemic it is crucial for me to be able to consistently travel to work to be able to care for my patients. On that morning, I was forced to wake up my family at 5:00 am to take me to work. My wife (who is also an RN working directly with COVID-19 patients and exhausted from work herself) and our two young children were required to take me to work each morning so they could be left with our other car for the day. Due to the garage door being stuck in the closed position, I called PCM—this is the only day I have had any sort of response out of them.  They begrudgingly sent someone out to force it open and I have since had to live with my garage door left open (it must be manually pushed, and only closes halfway).  The assistant manager at the time apologized and acknowledged how unacceptable this was, and I was left with his assurance that he would remind his boss to resolve the issue promptly.  Several months have now past and my garage is still broken and unsecured.

You may be wondering why a tenant is dealing with this instead of the property owner.  This is only because my landlord—in tears—informed me that she has been attempting to communicate with both PCM and WVA, but has been brushed off and even ignored every time whilst attempting to be the trustworthy and ethical person she is. She is elderly and retired, using English as her second language, and she has had immense difficulty navigating your broken system. I have stepped forward and offered to handle the situation for her due to the stress this has been causing her. I am an excellent tenant, never being late or missing a rent payment in my three years of residency here, and I deserve to have a reliable and secure garage door to secure my belongings.
The handling of this issue is unacceptable. My landlord only requires a simple approval to be obtained from you, and the fact that your company has repeatedly ignored that request is ridiculous and neglectful. I expect the door to be replaced and left entirely in working order by Friday, July 24, 2020 or we will be exploring legal options to resolve this matter.
Do the right thing.</review>

BEFORE VISITING THIS PRACTICE, PLEASE READ ON.
Completely unhelpful, both for long-standing health concerns I had from before and trivial issues alike. She never was able to resolve my problems or even say anything useful about them. I saw Dr. Amersi for a total of 10 minutes during which time she refused to acknowledge or inspect lab results I had done just prior to my appointment because of which I was referred to a specialist, and refused to discuss my concerns and my medical history in detail despite never having met me before. She kept dismissing all of the information I shared with her as seemingly unimportant, insisting I would have to come back several times over the next few months for separate appointments. Office wait is more than an hour for a 10-minute consultation. Blood work is sort of done in the back in an open space, looked and felt very unprofessional. Staff is always claiming to be "really busy", NEVER follow up over the phone, NEVER email pertinent information they PROMISE to send, NEVER respond in a timely manner, NEVER reachable. Always rude and unprofessional, taking forever to look up past visits information over the phone, always having to "check with" someone else before they answer a question about any of the prior visits. EXTREMELY INCOMPETENT AND UNTRUSTWORTHY. Expect a WRONG AND OVERCHARGED BILL - my first invoice from this office contained radiology tests for over $1,000 which I have NEVER done. First prescription from this office "HAD TO" be fulfilled by a local pharmacy that had no official website and did not exist in my insurance's directory; I was contacted by them by phone to provide shipping information. Instead of shipping my prescription, someone contacted me REPEATEDLY by phone AND text at very inappropriate hours (after 9PM on Friday and Saturday) to ask if I can "meet them outside my building to receive my prescription". I stated I am uncomfortable with that and preferred my medication to be shipped; however, no luck - I got another call AND text from a random person stating they "received my medication by mistake" and asking if I have theirs instead (??!!), and then another call AND many texts from the pharmacy person TELLING me (yes, telling, not asking) that they ENTERED MY BUILDING WITHOUT MY CONSENT AND DROPPED OFF MY PRESCRIPTION AT MY DOOR - while I was actually home, which felt beyond creepy and invasive. I do not understand why this prescription could not be fulfilled at a standard CVS. I do not trust Dr. Amersi and any of her affiliations.<//review>

<review>Ok. In this review, I need to add a bit of back-story in order to let readers understand why we like Dr. Amersi so much. And to also let others know that extensive research is needed before you make life-changing decisions regarding high-risk pregnancies.

In April of 2016, my wife had received a couple of vaccines. One if them was the MMR vaccine, which is not recommended during early pregnancy. She did not know she was pregnant at the time so you can imagine how scared and upset we were when we found out she was pregnant during the time she received the vaccine. After discovering she was pregnant, we scheduled an appointment with an OB-GYN in West LA. It was one of the saddest doctor visits I had ever gone to. The news/info we received from that doctor was upsetting and horrifying. He recommended we terminate the pregnancy and also said he would do it. He went on to mention that we needed to do it right away and told us to schedule the termination as soon as possible. It was the last thing we wanted to hear. On our way home after the appointment, I tried to conduct a bit of research regarding the effects of the MMR vaccine during pregnancy via Google but for some strange reason we couldn’t get service on our phones. You can imagine how upset we were on our ride home.

As soon as we got home, I went straight to my computer to conduct research on the MMR vaccine and found what it can theoretically do to an unborn child and pregnant mother. What I found was a mix of petrifying and wipe-the-sweat-from-forehead info. My wife and I talked about it for a couple of hours and decided we were going to schedule more doctor appointments to get peace of mind and to make sure everything was going to be 100% fine. Of course, I conducted more research on business review websites in order to find the right doctors since our previous experience had been heartbreaking. It was a must. Well, research is always a must. One of the doctors we found was Shamsah Amersi, MD. Keep in mind that we did see other doctors after we visited Dr. Amersi.

It started with a call to her office, which was answered by a helpful staff member (Wendy). I expressed how concerned we were about the situation and that we were planning on seeing other doctors as well. Wendy kindly let me know there was a two-week waiting period to see the doctor but mentioned she would call me if someone canceled an appointment. And of course, she did. Wendy called me the next day. When we first met with Dr. Amersi and told her about everything my wife was going through, she immediately let us know that everything was going to be ok. She also gave my wife a hug and told her not to worry. Dr. Amersi is personable, compassionate, caring, professional, knowledgeable, a sweetheart, and a great doctor. We saw a few more doctors after that but my wife said she felt good about Dr. Amersi. As you can guess, we decided Dr. Amersi was going to be the doctor we stay with. During our second visit to her office, she informed us that a lot of tests would be conducted in order to make sure the baby was fine. And yes, there were a lot of tests. Considering that she has a busy office, her staff ensured my wife’s office visits were smooth and stress-free. It speaks volumes about the professionalism of her staff/team. Throughout the pregnancy, we were always able to get our questions answered either by a call back or via email from Dr. Amersi. During our office visits, she always made it a point to ask us if we had any questions or concerns and would take the time to sit with us and talk about them.

My wife gave birth to a beautiful healthy girl and I am writing this from the hospital room we are in. Dr. Amersi has visited my wife a few times already to check on her and the baby. We are very happy that we met her and decided to stay with her.<//review>< pictures>

<rating>5< /rating>< Review>
I have seen Dr. Amersi for the past six years or so and really love her. She is super knowledgable and easy to talk to. She works with you to figure out what the best birth control option is for you and your future plans. She thinks ahead and asks questions to make sure she is familiar with your situation. She has never been judgmental about my sex life, and I have referred several friends to her who all love her as well. She often relates herself to your personal experience, which I find very refreshing and personable (as well as extremely comforting). She does everything she can to make you feel comfortable in what can often be a not-so-comfortable situation.

I also love that she doesn't make me feel like a cash cow. I have been to OBGYNs who make you get a pregnancy test every time you are there (Umm...I can tell you 100% I am NOT pregnant) and make you come in and wait more than an hour to see the doctor just to be told you have an abnormal test result of some sort and have to come BACK in (and probably wait another hour) to get treated. Dr. Amersi has NEVER been like that. I get in and out in less than an hour (most of the time in a half hour), and she takes time to talk to me when I have questions and gives me all the information about any medications or procedures I need. She doesn't push pills (actually has asked me to go off or switch BCs when she is worried about the effects the hormones are having on my body and the impact it will have on my ability to have children in the future...I love that she thinks ahead like that).

Anyways, I can't say enough great things about Dr. Amersi and her staff.<//Review>

<Review>Although she wasn’t my first choice (as my top choices were not taking on new patients), I chose Dr. Amersi because she was affiliated with Santa Monica UCLA, the hospital where I was planning to give birth. I was also under the impression that I’d feel more comfortable with a female doctor and would be better off with one that was exclusive to her patients all the way up to the delivery date. I thought I’d build more of a relationship and receive better attention, but this is not what I found. Not only was Dr. Amersi’s bedside manner terse and insincere, but I found she rushed me out of every appointment, and any questions and concerns I had were never fully answered. When I started to have some medical concerns later on in my pregnancy, she didn’t follow up about them at my next appointment only days later. Her lack of communication culminated in the discovery in my ninth month of pregnancy that she had given up her privileges to Santa Monica UCLA and wouldn’t be able to deliver my baby there. She didn’t share this information with me until I insisted she go over some questions I had for her and it accidentally came to light. This meant I had to find a new OB three weeks before my delivery date! Dr. Amersi and her practice don’t offer the opportunity for building trust between doctor and patient, and coupled with the ongoing admin fees, the entire operation feels less concerned with patient care than it does with taking on as many patients as possible (and making money).< /Review>< Response>
